Another diamond in the rough. It was small but cozy. Great staff, they got me all the extras I asked for, extra napkins, salsa for chips and pico de gio.  Waitress recommended the steak Fajita salad and it was exactly what I needed.

Washed it down with the bucket sized cup of Pepsi finished up the salsa and chips.

Place is simple and the food is good. I will definitely try to make it back here in the future. Place I delivered was literally across the street so very convenient.

Only glitch and not a big deal is washroom can only be accessed from outside.
LOL!  But it was clean, well stocked and didn't stink and no plumbing issues.<//text>

< Review>
I sought out a 3rd option after the IRS only gave me two repayment options that didn't fit my financial ability. Platinum Tax Defenders takes $500 to open your investigation, and suggests that they may be able to reduce the amount you have to pay back. The details were vague, but I get it, every case is different. I paid the fee and over the course of the next few weeks, we exchanged forms and information to get the investigation started. I was told the $500 would be a one-time fee that covered EVERYTHING. I was also told I'd be issued a case manager that I would deal with one-on-one. I dealt with a different person EVERY time. Finally they offered me a resolution that would require that I go into a "current but not collectible" status, which essentially means they would collect from my subsequent returns. I agreed to this, and then they notified me of a "resolution fee" of $350. This was the first mention of this fee throughout the entire process. I reluctantly paid it. Immediately after my payment was accepted, they told me that I actually didn't qualify for this program, and set me up with an immediate 6-year repayment plan. I feel like I've been completely scammed. Lies upon lies upon lies. Avoid this company at all costs, they act in a predatory and suspicious way.

They eventually agreed to do my 2016 taxes ‚Äúas a courtesy‚Äù (even their agreement said this would be covered, so no, it‚Äôs not considered a courtesy to provide a service for which I paid), but I was still on my own for 2017.

< Text>
Mixed experiences, depends on what you need and who you encounter.  I recently had a pleasant experience when I was shopping for a hairdryer.  I am accustomed to the better lines of hairdryers, so I had a price point in mind.  As I was browsing the selection, a salon rep approached me and asked if she could help.  Based on my request, she helped me understand the terminology between the different models, and what might be best for my hair.  Then she asked what my budget was, and did in fact help me stick to my budget, which I sincerely appreciated.  I hate being up-sold.
On other visits I've felt less helped and at times steered toward more expensive items than I wanted to get.  So all in all it's a mixed bag.
Once in a while when they have sales on the brand-name items you can get a pretty good deal.  I also like taking advantage of using my Ulta Rewards points toward purchases.  The cashiers are usually helpful to tell me if/when my points are going to expire so I can use them.  The rewards points have taken some serious $$ off of my total when I've let them accumulate.</Text>
